</table>
<p><b>Clube Atlético Mineiro</b> (<small>Brazilian Portuguese: </small><span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_Portuguese" title="Help:IPA for Portuguese">[ˈklubi atˈlɛtʃiku miˈnejɾu]</a></span>), commonly known as <b>Atlético Mineiro</b> or <b>Atlético</b>, and colloquially as <b>Galo</b> (<small>pronounced: </small><span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_Portuguese" title="Help:IPA for Portuguese">[ˈgalu]</a></span>, "Rooster"), is a professional <a href="/wiki/Football_team" title="Football team">football club</a> based in <a href="/wiki/Belo_Horizonte" title="Belo Horizonte">Belo Horizonte</a>, <a href="/wiki/Minas_Gerais" title="Minas Gerais">Minas Gerais</a>, Brazil. The team competes in the <a href="/wiki/Campeonato_Brasileiro_S%C3%A9rie_A" title="Campeonato Brasileiro Série A">Campeonato Brasileiro Série A</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_football_league_system" title="Brazilian football league system">first level</a> of Brazilian football, as well as in the <a href="/wiki/Campeonato_Mineiro" title="Campeonato Mineiro">Campeonato Mineiro</a>, the top tier <a href="/wiki/State_football_leagues_in_Brazil" title="State football leagues in Brazil">state league</a> of Minas Gerais.</p>
<p>Atlético Mineiro is the oldest active football club in Minas Gerais, founded on 25 March 1908 by twenty-two students from Belo Horizonte.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Atl.C3.A9tico_-_Hist.C3.B3ria_-_Funda.C3.A7.C3.A3o_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-Atl.C3.A9tico_-_Hist.C3.B3ria_-_Funda.C3.A7.C3.A3o-3">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup> Despite having liberal, upper-class founders, the club opened its doors to players of every <a href="/wiki/Social_class" title="Social class">social class</a>, establishing itself as a "people's club",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pc1_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-pc1-5">[5]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pc2_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-pc2-6">[6]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> and becoming one of the most supported in Brazil.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:2_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-:2-8">[8]</a></sup> The club's mascot, a rooster, has been strongly associated with Atlético since its introduction in the 1930s. Over the years, the word <i>galo</i> (<a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">Portuguese</a> for "rooster") became a common nickname for the club itself. The team's regular home <a href="/wiki/Kit_(association_football)" title="Kit (association football)">kit</a> comprises black-and-white striped shirts, with black shorts and white socks.</p>
<p>Atlético has won the Campeonato Mineiro a record 43 times. At national level, the club has won the Campeonato Brasileiro once and has finished second on five occasions. Atlético has also won one <a href="/wiki/Copa_do_Brasil" title="Copa do Brasil">Copa do Brasil</a>, one <a href="/wiki/Copa_dos_Campe%C3%B5es_Estaduais" title="Copa dos Campeões Estaduais">Copa dos Campeões Estaduais</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Copa_dos_Campe%C3%B5es_da_Copa_Brasil" title="Copa dos Campeões da Copa Brasil">Copa dos Campeões Brasileiros</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-:0-9">[9]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:1_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-:1-10">[10]</a></sup> In <a href="/wiki/Clube_Atl%C3%A9tico_Mineiro_in_international_club_football" title="Clube Atlético Mineiro in international club football">international club football</a>, Atlético has won the <a href="/wiki/Copa_Libertadores" title="Copa Libertadores">Copa Libertadores</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Recopa_Sudamericana" title="Recopa Sudamericana">Recopa Sudamericana</a> once each, and a record two <a href="/wiki/Copa_CONMEBOL" title="Copa CONMEBOL">Copa CONMEBOL</a>; the team has also reached three other continental finals. The club has also competed in other sports throughout its history, with the <a href="/wiki/Futsal" title="Futsal">futsal</a> department becoming especially notable.</p>
<p>The club plays the majority of its home matches at the <a href="/wiki/Est%C3%A1dio_Independ%C3%AAncia" title="Estádio Independência">Independência</a>, while the <a href="/wiki/Mineir%C3%A3o" title="Mineirão">Mineirão</a> — the club's ground for most of its history — is used as Galo's home in important and high-attendance matches.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> Atlético has a long-standing cross-city rivalry with <a href="/wiki/Cruzeiro_Esporte_Clube" title="Cruzeiro Esporte Clube">Cruzeiro</a>, with matches between the two teams referred to as the <a href="/wiki/Cl%C3%A1ssico_Mineiro" title="Clássico Mineiro">Clássico Mineiro</a>. The club also holds a <a href="/wiki/Am%C3%A9rica_Futebol_Clube%E2%80%93Clube_Atl%C3%A9tico_Mineiro_rivalry" title="América Futebol Clube–Clube Atlético Mineiro rivalry">local rivalry</a> with <a href="/wiki/Am%C3%A9rica_Futebol_Clube_(MG)" title="América Futebol Clube (MG)">América Mineiro</a>, and an <a href="/wiki/Clube_de_Regatas_do_Flamengo%E2%80%93Clube_Atl%C3%A9tico_Mineiro_rivalry" title="Clube de Regatas do Flamengo–Clube Atlético Mineiro rivalry">interstate one</a> with <a href="/wiki/Clube_de_Regatas_do_Flamengo" title="Clube de Regatas do Flamengo">Flamengo</a>. Atlético has the eighth most valuable brand in Brazil, worth <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_real" title="Brazilian real">R$</a>515.5 million (€143 million) as of 2016, and ranks seventh in the country in terms of turnover, generating R$244.6 million (€62.2 million) in 2015.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:6_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-:6-12">[12]</a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Clube_Atl%C3%A9tico_Mineiro&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Clube_Atl%C3%A9tico_Mineiro" title="History of Clube Atlético Mineiro">History of Clube Atlético Mineiro</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_years_and_achievements_.281908.E2.80.9349.29">Early years and achievements (1908–49)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Clube_Atl%C3%A9tico_Mineiro&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Early years and achievements (1908–49)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Galo-1914.jpg"><img alt="Football players in uniform and other men in suits" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="403" data-file-width="843" height="105" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Galo-1914.jpg/220px-Galo-1914.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Galo-1914.jpg/330px-Galo-1914.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Galo-1914.jpg/440px-Galo-1914.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Galo-1914.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Atlético Mineiro team that won the Taça Bueno Brandão in 1914, the club's first trophy.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Atlético Mineiro was formed on 25 March 1908 by a group of twenty-two students from <a href="/wiki/Belo_Horizonte" title="Belo Horizonte">Belo Horizonte</a>, who decided the club's name would be <i>Athletico Mineiro Foot Ball Club.</i> The club's first match was played against Sport Club Futebol on 21 March 1909; Atlético won 3–0, with the first goal scored by <a href="/wiki/An%C3%ADbal_Machado" title="Aníbal Machado">Aníbal Machado</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Atl.C3.A9tico_-_Hist.C3.B3ria_-_Funda.C3.A7.C3.A3o_3-1"><a href="#cite_note-Atl.C3.A9tico_-_Hist.C3.B3ria_-_Funda.C3.A7.C3.A3o-3">[3]</a></sup> In 1913, the club's name was officially changed to <i>Clube Atlético Mineiro</i>, and in the following year Atlético won the Taça Bueno Brandão, the first competition ever held in the state of Minas Gerais.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> In 1915, the club won the inaugural edition of the <a href="/wiki/Campeonato_Mineiro" title="Campeonato Mineiro">Campeonato Mineiro</a>, the <a href="/wiki/State_football_leagues_in_Brazil" title="State football leagues in Brazil">state league</a> of Minas Gerais. The competition was then organised by the <i>Liga Mineira de Sports Athléticos</i>, which would later become the <a href="/wiki/Federa%C3%A7%C3%A3o_Mineira_de_Futebol" title="Federação Mineira de Futebol">Federação Mineira de Futebol</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Am%C3%A9rica_Futebol_Clube_(MG)" title="América Futebol Clube (MG)">América</a> won the next ten editions of the Mineiro, and Atlético only won the league again in 1926, led by striker <a href="/wiki/M%C3%A1rio_de_Castro" title="Mário de Castro">Mário de Castro</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> In 1927, forwards <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Said_Paulo_Arges&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Said Paulo Arges (page does not exist)">Said</a> and <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Jairo_de_Assis_Almeida&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Jairo de Assis Almeida (page does not exist)">Jairo</a> joined Castro to form an attacking partnership nicknamed the <i>Trio Maldito</i> ("Unholy Trio"), which guided Atlético to another state league triumph.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> In 1929, the club played its first international encounter, against Portuguese club against <a href="/wiki/Vit%C3%B3ria_F.C." title="Vitória F.C.">Vitória de Setúbal</a>, winning 3–1 in a match played at the <a href="/wiki/Est%C3%A1dio_Presidente_Ant%C3%B4nio_Carlos" title="Estádio Presidente Antônio Carlos">Presidente Antônio Carlos Stadium</a>. The ground had opened earlier that year, and would be the club's home for the following two decades.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hist.C3.B3ria_-_Atl.C3.A9tico_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-Hist.C3.B3ria_-_Atl.C3.A9tico-18">[18]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Clube_Atl%C3%A9tico_Mineiro_1937.jpg"><img alt="Football team photo on the pitch" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="403" data-file-width="843" height="105" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Clube_Atl%C3%A9tico_Mineiro_1937.jpg/220px-Clube_Atl%C3%A9tico_Mineiro_1937.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Clube_Atl%C3%A9tico_Mineiro_1937.jpg/330px-Clube_Atl%C3%A9tico_Mineiro_1937.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Clube_Atl%C3%A9tico_Mineiro_1937.jpg/440px-Clube_Atl%C3%A9tico_Mineiro_1937.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Clube_Atl%C3%A9tico_Mineiro_1937.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/1937_Copa_dos_Campe%C3%B5es_Estaduais" title="1937 Copa dos Campeões Estaduais">1937 Copa dos Campeões Estaduais</a> winning squad</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Atlético won the state league in 1931 and 1932, before becoming a professional club in 1933.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> After another Campeonato Mineiro triumph in 1936, Atlético won the <a href="/wiki/Copa_dos_Campe%C3%B5es_Estaduais" title="Copa dos Campeões Estaduais">Copa dos Campeões Estaduais</a> in <a href="/wiki/1937_Copa_dos_Campe%C3%B5es_Estaduais" title="1937 Copa dos Campeões Estaduais">1937</a>, its first title at national level. The competition was organised by the <i>Federação Brasileira de Foot-Ball</i>, a federation for professional clubs that would later merge into the <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_Football_Confederation" title="Brazilian Football Confederation">Brazilian Sports Confederation</a> (CBD). The Copa dos Campeões Estaduais was contested by the 1936 state league champions from Minas Gerais (Atlético), <a href="/wiki/Campeonato_Carioca" title="Campeonato Carioca">Rio de Janeiro</a> (<a href="/wiki/Fluminense_FC" title="Fluminense FC">Fluminense</a>), <a href="/wiki/Campeonato_Paulista" title="Campeonato Paulista">São Paulo</a> (<a href="/wiki/Associa%C3%A7%C3%A3o_Portuguesa_de_Desportos" title="Associação Portuguesa de Desportos">Portuguesa</a>) and <a href="/wiki/Campeonato_Capixaba" title="Campeonato Capixaba">Espírito Santo</a> (<a href="/wiki/Rio_Branco_Atl%C3%A9tico_Clube" title="Rio Branco Atlético Clube">Rio Branco</a>). Atlético defeated the latter 5–1 in the final match, played at the Antônio Carlos stadium.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup> <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Guaracy_Januzzi&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Guaracy Januzzi (page does not exist)">Guará</a> rose as the club's top player during that period,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> and the interstate title was followed by two more Campeonato Mineiro victories, in 1938 and 1939.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:03_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-:03-22">[22]</a></sup></p>
<p>Success continued in the 1940s, with a squad that included <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Carlyle_Guimar%C3%A3es_Cardoso&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Carlyle Guimarães Cardoso (page does not exist)">Carlyle</a>, <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Lucas_Miranda&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Lucas Miranda (page does not exist)">Lucas Miranda</a>, <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=N%C3%ADvio_Gabrich&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Nívio Gabrich (page does not exist)">Nívio</a> and goalkeeper <a href="/wiki/Kafunga" title="Kafunga">Kafunga</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> The club was dominant in the state as it won the league in 1941, 1942, 1946, 1947 and 1949.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:03_22-1"><a href="#cite_note-:03-22">[22]</a></sup> Although América had been Atlético's long-standing adversary, a new <a href="/wiki/Cl%C3%A1ssico_Mineiro" title="Clássico Mineiro">rivalry</a> started to develop with <a href="/wiki/Cruzeiro_Esporte_Clube" title="Cruzeiro Esporte Clube">Cruzeiro</a> in the 1940s, as it became Galo's main challenger during this period.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fifa_1-1"><a href="#cite_note-fifa-1">[1]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="European_tour_and_the_Mineir.C3.A3o_era_.281950.E2.80.9369.29">European tour and the Mineirão era (1950–69)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Clube_Atl%C3%A9tico_Mineiro&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: European tour and the Mineirão era (1950–69)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/1950_Atl%C3%A9tico_Mineiro_European_tour" title="1950 Atlético Mineiro European tour">1950 Atlético Mineiro European tour</a></div>
<p>In 1950, the club's home moved from the Antônio Carlos to the newer and larger <a href="/wiki/Est%C3%A1dio_Independ%C3%AAncia" title="Estádio Independência">Estádio Independência</a>. The season saw another Campeonato Mineiro triumph and the club's first <a href="/wiki/1950_Atl%C3%A9tico_Mineiro_European_tour" title="1950 Atlético Mineiro European tour">European tour</a>, in which it played ten games in five countries. The excursion happened at a time when there were neither regular national competitions in Brazil nor continental ones in South America, and followed soon after the traumatic <a href="/wiki/Uruguay_v_Brazil_(1950_FIFA_World_Cup)" title="Uruguay v Brazil (1950 FIFA World Cup)">Maracanazo</a>. The tour and Atlético's results, many of which achieved under adverse weather conditions and snow, were seen by national sports media as a historic achievement for <a href="/wiki/Football_in_Brazil" title="Football in Brazil">Brazilian football</a> itself.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> The team, captained by <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Jos%C3%A9_do_Monte_Furtado_Sobrinho&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="José do Monte Furtado Sobrinho (page does not exist)">Zé do Monte</a>, was dubbed the <i>Campeões do Gelo</i> ("Ice Champions"), a title that is remembered in the club's official anthem.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:5_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-:5-26">[26]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> The club's success in the state competition continued in the 1950s, a decade that saw the rise of forward <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Ubaldo_Miranda&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Ubaldo Miranda (page does not exist)">Ubaldo</a> and five consecutive Campeonato Mineiro victories from 1952 to 1956. After another state league title in 1958, Atlético took part in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1959_Ta%C3%A7a_Brasil" title="1959 Taça Brasil">inaugural edition</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Ta%C3%A7a_Brasil" title="Taça Brasil">Taça Brasil</a> in the following year, reaching the third round.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> The tournament, the country's first annual nationwide competition, was a <a href="/wiki/Single-elimination_tournament" title="Single-elimination tournament">cup</a> contested between state league champions, originally created by the CBD to select Brazil's entrants in the newly formed <a href="/wiki/Copa_Libertadores" title="Copa Libertadores">Copa Libertadores</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:13_29-0"><a href="#cite_note-:13-29">[29]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the 1960s, Atlético won the Campeonato Mineiro twice, in 1962 and 1963, but failed to advance to the later stages of the Taça Brasil. <a href="/wiki/Mineir%C3%A3o" title="Mineirão">Mineirão</a>, Belo Horizonte's new stadium, opened in 1965 and immediately became the club's home. It was in the mid-1960s that the rivalry with Cruzeiro became the biggest in the state, after this club won the first five state leagues of the Mineirão era. In 1967, another national-level competition was created by the CBD, the <a href="/wiki/Torneio_Roberto_Gomes_Pedrosa" title="Torneio Roberto Gomes Pedrosa">Torneio Roberto Gomes Pedrosa</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:13_29-1"><a href="#cite_note-:13-29">[29]</a></sup> It included more clubs than the Taça Brasil, but Atlético did not finish in the top-four in any of its editions in the decade. In the second half of the 1960s, highlights came in the form of friendlies against national sides. In 1968, Atlético, representing the <a href="/wiki/Brazil_national_football_team" title="Brazil national football team">Brazilian national team</a>, defeated <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_1968" title="UEFA Euro 1968">European Championship runners-up</a> <a href="/wiki/Yugoslavia_national_football_team" title="Yugoslavia national football team">Yugoslavia</a> 3–2 at the Mineirão;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> the following year, the <i>Seleção</i> itself, which would become champions of the <a href="/wiki/1970_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1970 FIFA World Cup">1970 FIFA World Cup</a>, was defeated 2–1.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="National_success_and_state_dominance_.281970.E2.80.9389.29">National success and state dominance (1970–89)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Clube_Atl%C3%A9tico_Mineiro&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: National success and state dominance (1970–89)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Dario_2014_01.jpg"><img alt="Middle-aged man smiling, with a football goal in the back" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="585" data-file-width="614" height="210" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Dario_2014_01.jpg/220px-Dario_2014_01.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Dario_2014_01.jpg/330px-Dario_2014_01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Dario_2014_01.jpg/440px-Dario_2014_01.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Dario_2014_01.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Dad%C3%A1_Maravilha" title="Dadá Maravilha">Dario</a>, here pictured in 2014, was the top goalscorer and led Galo to triumph in the <a href="/wiki/1971_Campeonato_Brasileiro_S%C3%A9rie_A" title="1971 Campeonato Brasileiro Série A">1971 Brasileirão</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>With the arrival of <a href="/wiki/Tel%C3%AA_Santana" title="Telê Santana">Telê Santana</a> as the club's head coach in 1970, Galo broke Cruzeiro's sequence and won its first state league title in the Mineirão,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> also finishing third in the last <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1970_Torneio_Roberto_Gomes_Pedrosa" title="1970 Torneio Roberto Gomes Pedrosa">Roberto Gomes Pedrosa</a>. In 1971, captained by midfielder <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Oldair_Barchi&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Oldair Barchi (page does not exist)">Oldair</a> and with <a href="/wiki/1970_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1970 FIFA World Cup">World Cup</a>-winning forward <a href="/wiki/Dad%C3%A1_Maravilha" title="Dadá Maravilha">Dario</a> as the league's top goalscorer, Atlético won the <a href="/wiki/1971_Campeonato_Brasileiro_S%C3%A9rie_A" title="1971 Campeonato Brasileiro Série A">Campeonato Brasileiro</a>. It was the first edition of the competition, also known as the Brasileirão, which replaced both the Taça Brasil and the Roberto Gomes Pedrosa as the new national championship.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:13_29-2"><a href="#cite_note-:13-29">[29]</a></sup> Atlético played a final group stage against <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Paulo_FC" title="São Paulo FC">São Paulo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Botafogo_de_Futebol_e_Regatas" title="Botafogo de Futebol e Regatas">Botafogo</a>, defeating the former 1–0 at the Mineirão and the latter 1–0 at the <a href="/wiki/Maracan%C3%A3_Stadium" title="Maracanã Stadium">Maracanã</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> The victory also secured the club's first participation in an official continental competition, the <a href="/wiki/1972_Copa_Libertadores" title="1972 Copa Libertadores">1972 Copa Libertadores</a>, in which it did not advance past the first group stage.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup></p>
<p>After four trophyless years, Atlético won the state league again in 1976 and finished third in the <a href="/wiki/1976_Campeonato_Brasileiro_S%C3%A9rie_A" title="1976 Campeonato Brasileiro Série A">Campeonato Brasileiro</a>. That season saw the emergence of a golden generation of players, formed in the club's youth academies under coach <a href="/wiki/Barbatana" title="Barbatana">Barbatana</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:10_36-0"><a href="#cite_note-:10-36">[36]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Reinaldo_de_Lima" title="José Reinaldo de Lima">Reinaldo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Toninho_Cerezo" title="Toninho Cerezo">Toninho Cerezo</a>, <a href="/wiki/%C3%89der_Aleixo_de_Assis" title="Éder Aleixo de Assis">Éder</a>, <a href="/wiki/Luiz_Carlos_Ferreira" title="Luiz Carlos Ferreira">Luizinho</a>, <a href="/wiki/Paulo_Isidoro" title="Paulo Isidoro">Paulo Isidoro</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jo%C3%A3o_Leite_da_Silva_Neto" title="João Leite da Silva Neto">João Leite</a>, players who represented Brazil at international level, were central to the team that took Atlético to six consecutive state league victories between 1978 and 1983, and to good results in the Série A.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> Atlético came second in the <a href="/wiki/1977_Campeonato_Brasileiro_S%C3%A9rie_A" title="1977 Campeonato Brasileiro Série A">1977 Brasileirão</a>, losing the final to São Paulo in a <a href="/wiki/Penalty_shootout" title="Penalty shootout">penalty shootout</a> at the Mineirão, despite remaining undefeated for the entire season. Reinaldo, the league's top scorer in that season with an average of 1.56 goals per match, was banned from the final. By his account, this was because of his insistence on celebrating his goals by raising his fist, a political symbol that opposed the <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_military_government" title="Brazilian military government">Brazilian military government</a> of the time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> In 1978, Atlético reached the <a href="/wiki/1978_Copa_Libertadores" title="1978 Copa Libertadores">Copa Libertadores</a> semi-finals and won the <a href="/wiki/Copa_dos_Campe%C3%B5es_da_Copa_Brasil" title="Copa dos Campeões da Copa Brasil">Copa dos Campeões Brasileiros</a>, a tournament organised by the CBD between past winners of the Brasileirão. In a repetition of the previous year's Brasileiro decisive match, the opponent in the final of this competition was São Paulo, with Atlético this time winning a penalty shootout.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:183px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:WC78_BRA-ITA.jpg"><img alt="Brazilian footballer being tackled from behind by an Italian player" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="148" data-file-width="181" height="148" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/a/a5/WC78_BRA-ITA.jpg" width="181"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:WC78_BRA-ITA.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Reinaldo_de_Lima" title="José Reinaldo de Lima">Reinaldo</a> (right), nicknamed <i>Rei</i> ("King"), is Atlético's all-time top goalscorer and was part of the club's golden generation.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/1980_Campeonato_Brasileiro_S%C3%A9rie_A" title="1980 Campeonato Brasileiro Série A">1980</a>, after having the best record in the first stages of the Brasileirão, Atlético lost to <a href="/wiki/Clube_de_Regatas_do_Flamengo" title="Clube de Regatas do Flamengo">Flamengo</a> in a controversial final of the competition. Three Galo players were sent off, among them Reinaldo, who received a straight red card after scoring twice.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:7_43-0"><a href="#cite_note-:7-43">[43]</a></sup> The team was then eliminated from the <a href="/wiki/1981_Copa_Libertadores" title="1981 Copa Libertadores">following year's Copa Libertadores</a> undefeated, in another decisive match marked by controversy: a play-off against Flamengo that ended after 37 minutes, following the sendings-off of five Atlético players.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:7_43-1"><a href="#cite_note-:7-43">[43]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> During the 1980s, the club participated in and won international friendly competitions, such as the <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam_Tournament" title="Amsterdam Tournament">Amsterdam Tournament</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Tournoi_de_Paris" title="Tournoi de Paris">Tournoi de Paris</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup> Atlético had the best statistic league records of the 1980, <a href="/wiki/1983_Campeonato_Brasileiro_S%C3%A9rie_A" title="1983 Campeonato Brasileiro Série A">1983</a>, <a href="/wiki/1985_Campeonato_Brasileiro_S%C3%A9rie_A" title="1985 Campeonato Brasileiro Série A">1985</a>, <a href="/wiki/1986_Campeonato_Brasileiro_S%C3%A9rie_A" title="1986 Campeonato Brasileiro Série A">1986</a> and <a href="/wiki/Copa_Uni%C3%A3o" title="Copa União">1987</a> Brasileirão seasons, but did not win the title, falling in the finals or semi-finals of those editions. In the second half of the decade, the club continued its success in the state, winning the Campeonato Mineiro in 1985, 1986, 1988 and 1989.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:03_22-2"><a href="#cite_note-:03-22">[22]</a></sup> Atlético was one of Brazil's top sides of the 1980s, providing many players to the Brazilian national team, being dominant at state level and having good performances in the Brasileiro, but a tendency to lose in its final knockout stages prevented a new title in this competition.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Continental_efforts_and_financial_turmoil_.281990.E2.80.932009.29">Continental efforts and financial turmoil (1990–2009)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Clube_Atl%C3%A9tico_Mineiro&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Continental efforts and financial turmoil (1990–2009)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In the following decade, Atlético won the state league in 1991 and first saw success at continental level in 1992, when it won the inaugural <a href="/wiki/1992_Copa_CONMEBOL" title="1992 Copa CONMEBOL">Copa CONMEBOL</a>. The team, managed by <a href="/wiki/Proc%C3%B3pio_Cardoso" title="Procópio Cardoso">Procópio Cardoso</a>, defeated Paraguay's <a href="/wiki/Club_Olimpia" title="Club Olimpia">Olimpia</a> in the finals to claim its first official international title.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup> As champion of that competition, the club took part in the <a href="/wiki/1993_Copa_de_Oro" title="1993 Copa de Oro">1993 Copa de Oro</a>, in which it eliminated rivals Cruzeiro in the semi-finals but eventually lost to Argentina's <a href="/wiki/Boca_Juniors" title="Boca Juniors">Boca Juniors</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup> After finishing fourth in the <a href="/wiki/1994_Campeonato_Brasileiro_S%C3%A9rie_A" title="1994 Campeonato Brasileiro Série A">1994 Brasileirão</a>, the following year saw the club win the state league and reach the finals of the <a href="/wiki/1995_Copa_CONMEBOL" title="1995 Copa CONMEBOL">Copa CONMEBOL</a> for a second time. This one ended in defeat to Argentine team <a href="/wiki/Rosario_Central" title="Rosario Central">Rosario Central</a> on penalties, after Atlético won the first leg by 4–0 and lost the second one by the same score.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> In 1996, Atlético participated in the <a href="/wiki/Copa_Master_de_CONMEBOL" title="Copa Master de CONMEBOL">Copa Masters CONMEBOL</a>, a competition between past winners of the Copa CONMEBOL that was played in <a href="/wiki/Cuiab%C3%A1" title="Cuiabá">Cuiabá</a>; Atlético eliminated Rosario Central in the semi-finals but lost to São Paulo in the final match.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup> The team also finished third in <a href="/wiki/1996_Campeonato_Brasileiro_S%C3%A9rie_A" title="1996 Campeonato Brasileiro Série A">that year's Brasileiro</a> and fourth in the <a href="/wiki/1997_Campeonato_Brasileiro_S%C3%A9rie_A" title="1997 Campeonato Brasileiro Série A">following edition</a>, falling in the semi-finals of both seasons. Another triumph came in the <a href="/wiki/1997_Copa_CONMEBOL" title="1997 Copa CONMEBOL">1997 Copa CONMEBOL</a>, when an Atlético team that included <a href="/wiki/Marques_Batista_de_Abreu" title="Marques Batista de Abreu">Marques</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cl%C3%A1udio_Taffarel" title="Cláudio Taffarel">Cláudio Taffarel</a> defeated Argentina's <a href="/wiki/Club_Atl%C3%A9tico_Lan%C3%BAs" title="Club Atlético Lanús">Lanús</a> in the finals, and won the trophy for a second time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:3_54-0"><a href="#cite_note-:3-54">[54]</a></sup> In 1999, after another Campeonato Mineiro title, a Galo side led by Marques and <a href="/wiki/Guilherme_de_C%C3%A1ssio_Alves" title="Guilherme de Cássio Alves">Guilherme</a>, the top scorer in the league, reached the <a href="/wiki/1999_Campeonato_Brasileiro_S%C3%A9rie_A" title="1999 Campeonato Brasileiro Série A">Série A</a> finals for the fourth time, but lost to <a href="/wiki/Sport_Club_Corinthians_Paulista" title="Sport Club Corinthians Paulista">Corinthians</a>. Despite international success and good performances in the Série A, the decade was marked by bad club administration by Atlético's presidents and deteriorating finances, which made the club one of the most indebted in Brazilian football.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2000, Atlético won the Campeonato Mineiro, reached the <a href="/wiki/2000_Copa_Libertadores" title="2000 Copa Libertadores">Copa Libertadores</a> quarter-finals and the semi-finals of <a href="/wiki/2000_Copa_Mercosur" title="2000 Copa Mercosur">Copa Mercosur</a>, but had a bad season in the national league, the <a href="/wiki/Copa_Jo%C3%A3o_Havelange" title="Copa João Havelange">Copa João Havelange</a>. The following year, despite a good performance in the <a href="/wiki/2001_Campeonato_Brasileiro_S%C3%A9rie_A" title="2001 Campeonato Brasileiro Série A">Brasileirão</a> with a squad that included Marques, Guilherme and <a href="/wiki/Gilberto_Silva" title="Gilberto Silva">Gilberto Silva</a>, the team again was eliminated in the competition's semi-finals, eventually finishing in fourth place. Atlético then finished in the upper part of the national league table in the following two seasons, but in <a href="/wiki/2004_Campeonato_Brasileiro_S%C3%A9rie_A" title="2004 Campeonato Brasileiro Série A">2004</a> it barely escaped relegation. In <a href="/wiki/2005_Campeonato_Brasileiro_S%C3%A9rie_A" title="2005 Campeonato Brasileiro Série A">2005</a> the club was demoted to the <a href="/wiki/Campeonato_Brasileiro_S%C3%A9rie_B" title="Campeonato Brasileiro Série B">Série B</a>, the second level of the Brasileirão.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-serieb_56-0"><a href="#cite_note-serieb-56">[56]</a></sup></p>
<p>With <a href="/wiki/Levir_Culpi" title="Levir Culpi">Levir Culpi</a> as head coach, the club won promotion at the first attempt as Série B champion in <a href="/wiki/2006_Campeonato_Brasileiro_S%C3%A9rie_B" title="2006 Campeonato Brasileiro Série B">2006</a>, returning to the Série A for the 2007 season.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-serieb_56-1"><a href="#cite_note-serieb-56">[56]</a></sup> That year, Atlético won the Campeonato Mineiro, its first trophy in seven years, and finished eighth in the <a href="/wiki/2007_Campeonato_Brasileiro_S%C3%A9rie_A" title="2007 Campeonato Brasileiro Série A">national league</a>. Alexandre Kalil was chosen as the club's new president in 2008, and tried to improve its finances and status.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup> In 2009, with <a href="/wiki/Diego_Tardelli" title="Diego Tardelli">Diego Tardelli</a> in good form, Galo led the <a href="/wiki/2009_Campeonato_Brasileiro_S%C3%A9rie_A" title="2009 Campeonato Brasileiro Série A">Brasileirão</a> for eight of the thirty-eight rounds, before eventually finishing in seventh place.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup> Despite some highlights at the beginning and end of the decade, the 2000s were not a successful period in the club's history, again marked by bad administration and frequent managerial changes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ronaldinho_2012_01.jpg"><img alt="Footballer preparing to kick a ball" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="500" data-file-width="474" height="232" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Ronaldinho_2012_01.jpg/220px-Ronaldinho_2012_01.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Ronaldinho_2012_01.jpg/330px-Ronaldinho_2012_01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Ronaldinho_2012_01.jpg/440px-Ronaldinho_2012_01.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ronaldinho_2012_01.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Ronaldinho" title="Ronaldinho">Ronaldinho</a> played an important part in the club's resurgence after his arrival in 2012.</div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Resurgence_and_international_success_.282010.E2.80.93.29">Resurgence and international success (2010–)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Clube_Atl%C3%A9tico_Mineiro&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Resurgence and international success (2010–)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The team won its 40th Campeonato Mineiro in 2010, but finished 13th in the <a href="/wiki/2010_Campeonato_Brasileiro_S%C3%A9rie_A" title="2010 Campeonato Brasileiro Série A">Série A</a>. After an unsuccessful year in <a href="/wiki/2011_Campeonato_Brasileiro_S%C3%A9rie_A" title="2011 Campeonato Brasileiro Série A">2011</a>, coming close to relegation, the arrival of <a href="/wiki/Cuca_(footballer)" title="Cuca (footballer)">Cuca</a> as head coach at the end of that season marked the beginning of another successful era for the club.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup> The club moved back to the Independência in 2012, as the Mineirão was closed for renovation, and won the <a href="/wiki/2012_Campeonato_Mineiro" title="2012 Campeonato Mineiro">Campeonato Mineiro</a> undefeated. The arrival of <a href="/wiki/Ronaldinho" title="Ronaldinho">Ronaldinho</a> in the middle of the season was an important event for the club,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> which eventually finished as runner-up in the <a href="/wiki/2012_Campeonato_Brasileiro_S%C3%A9rie_A" title="2012 Campeonato Brasileiro Série A">Série A</a> and earned a spot in the <a href="/wiki/2013_Copa_Libertadores" title="2013 Copa Libertadores">following year's Copa Libertadores</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup></p>
<p>Diego Tardelli and Gilberto Silva returned to the club in 2013, and joined Ronaldinho, <a href="/wiki/J%C3%B4" title="Jô">Jô</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bernard_(footballer)" title="Bernard (footballer)">Bernard</a> towards another <a href="/wiki/2013_Campeonato_Mineiro" title="2013 Campeonato Mineiro">Campeonato Mineiro</a> triumph. The quarter-finals of that season's Copa Libertadores saw an iconic moment for Atlético, when a penalty kick was awarded to Mexican <a href="/wiki/Club_Tijuana" title="Club Tijuana">Club Tijuana</a> in <a href="/wiki/Overtime_(sports)" title="Overtime (sports)">injury time</a>. It would have meant elimination if it had been scored, but was saved by Atlético's goalkeeper <a href="/wiki/Victor_Leandro_Bagy" title="Victor Leandro Bagy">Victor</a> with his foot. The save, according to sports commentators and fans, represented the "kicking out" of the club's historic "jinx".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup> Atlético then defeated Argentina's <a href="/wiki/Newell%27s_Old_Boys" title="Newell's Old Boys">Newell's Old Boys</a> in the semi-finals and Olimpia in the <a href="/wiki/2013_Copa_Libertadores_Finals" title="2013 Copa Libertadores Finals">finals</a> on penalties, after losing both first legs by 2–0 and winning the second ones by the same score, to claim its first Copa Libertadores title.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup> The club's participation in the <a href="/wiki/2013_FIFA_Club_World_Cup" title="2013 FIFA Club World Cup">FIFA Club World Cup</a> was unsuccessful, as it failed to reach the final, losing to Moroccan hosts <a href="/wiki/Raja_Casablanca" title="Raja Casablanca">Raja Casablanca</a>; Atlético eventually finished in third place after defeating China's <a href="/wiki/Guangzhou_Evergrande_Taobao_F.C." title="Guangzhou Evergrande Taobao F.C.">Guangzhou Evergrande</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup></p>
<p>Under Levir Culpi, who returned to the club in 2014, Atlético won its first <a href="/wiki/Recopa_Sudamericana" title="Recopa Sudamericana">Recopa Sudamericana</a>, defeating Lanús for the second time in a continental <a href="/wiki/2014_Recopa_Sudamericana" title="2014 Recopa Sudamericana">final</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CONMEBOL_70-0"><a href="#cite_note-CONMEBOL-70">[70]</a></sup> In that season's <a href="/wiki/2014_Copa_do_Brasil" title="2014 Copa do Brasil">Copa do Brasil</a>, after trailing 0–3 on aggregate in both the quarter-finals and semi-finals (against Corinthians and Flamengo, respectively), Atlético made 4–3 comebacks and advanced.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> The competition's finals were the first at national level to feature the Belo Horizonte rivals, and Atlético defeated Cruzeiro on both encounters to win its first Copa do Brasil.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FourFourTwo_73-0"><a href="#cite_note-FourFourTwo-73">[73]</a></sup> The club's successful run in the decade continued in <a href="/wiki/2015_Clube_Atl%C3%A9tico_Mineiro_season" title="2015 Clube Atlético Mineiro season">2015</a>, when it won its 43rd <a href="/wiki/2015_Campeonato_Mineiro" title="2015 Campeonato Mineiro">Campeonato Mineiro</a> and finished second in the <a href="/wiki/2015_Campeonato_Brasileiro_S%C3%A9rie_A" title="2015 Campeonato Brasileiro Série A">Campeonato Brasileiro</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup> In <a href="/wiki/2016_Clube_Atl%C3%A9tico_Mineiro_season" title="2016 Clube Atlético Mineiro season">2016</a>, however, Atlético Mineiro ended the season without official trophies, finishing as runner-up of the <a href="/wiki/2016_Campeonato_Mineiro" title="2016 Campeonato Mineiro">Campeonato Mineiro</a> and the <a href="/wiki/2016_Copa_do_Brasil" title="2016 Copa do Brasil">Copa do Brasil</a>, and in fourth place in the <a href="/wiki/2016_Campeonato_Brasileiro_S%C3%A9rie_A" title="2016 Campeonato Brasileiro Série A">Brasileiro</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Symbols_and_colours">Symbols and colours</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Clube_Atl%C3%A9tico_Mineiro&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Symbols and colours">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Atl%C3%A9tico_Mineiro_crest_1910.svg"><img alt="Club badge: the letters CAM in black, written in an oval shape" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="953" data-file-width="1280" height="164" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Atl%C3%A9tico_Mineiro_crest_1910.svg/220px-Atl%C3%A9tico_Mineiro_crest_1910.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Atl%C3%A9tico_Mineiro_crest_1910.svg/330px-Atl%C3%A9tico_Mineiro_crest_1910.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Atl%C3%A9tico_Mineiro_crest_1910.svg/440px-Atl%C3%A9tico_Mineiro_crest_1910.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Atl%C3%A9tico_Mineiro_crest_1910.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The first crest used by Atlético Mineiro</div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Crest">Crest</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Clube_Atl%C3%A9tico_Mineiro&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Crest">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The club's first emblem, introduced in the 1910s, consisted of a simple design of the three initials of the club's name ("CAM" for Clube Atlético Mineiro) in an oval shape in black. The first and most significant change occurred in 1922, when an edged shield format was adopted, with the letters in its upper part and black and white stripes in the lower.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup> The crest's general appearance has been kept ever since, with only the exact format and the placement of the black and white stripes within the escutcheon changing over the decades. In the 1970s a golden <a href="/wiki/Star_(football_badge)" title="Star (football badge)">star</a> above the badge was introduced, alluding to the 1971 Série A title, which still remains.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup> Red stars were featured on two occasions, referring to the 1978 Copa dos Campeões and the 1992 and 1997 Copa CONMEBOL victories, but these were removed in 1999.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Galo_Doido_2012_01.jpg"><img alt="A person costumed as a rooster in a football uniform" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="472" data-file-width="428" height="243" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Galo_Doido_2012_01.jpg/220px-Galo_Doido_2012_01.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Galo_Doido_2012_01.jpg/330px-Galo_Doido_2012_01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/1/11/Galo_Doido_2012_01.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Galo_Doido_2012_01.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<i>Galo Doido</i> ("Crazy Rooster"), the club's stadium mascot.</div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mascot">Mascot</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Clube_Atl%C3%A9tico_Mineiro&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Mascot">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Atlético's mascot, a rooster, is one of the best-known in the country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup> According to <a href="/wiki/Kafunga" title="Kafunga">Kafunga</a>, who played as goalkeeper for the club from 1935 to 1955, the "rooster" nickname was associated with Atlético because of its kit colours.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup> In 1945, Fernando Pierucetti, known as Mangabeira, a cartoonist for the <i>A Folha de Minas</i> newspaper, was selected to design mascots for each of the three biggest clubs in Belo Horizonte. According to Mangabeira, Atlético's would be the rooster because the team used to play with passion and would never give up until the end of each match, like <a href="/wiki/Gamecock" title="Gamecock">gamecocks</a> in <a href="/wiki/Cockfight" title="Cockfight">cockfights</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup></p>
<p>Over the years, the word <i>galo</i> (<a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">Portuguese</a> for "rooster") became a cheering chant for the supporters and a nickname by which they referred to the club, an appellation that eventually spread to other football fans in the country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup> The nickname was incorporated into the club's official anthem, composed by Vicente Motta in 1968, whose chorus hails Atlético as a "strong and avenging rooster".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:5_26-1"><a href="#cite_note-:5-26">[26]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup> In 1976, a costumed rooster mascot was introduced, to accompany players and children in the match entrance. The stadium mascot was reintroduced with a new costume in 2005, named <i>Galo Doido</i> ("Crazy Rooster") by the supporters.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Kits">Kits</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Clube_Atl%C3%A9tico_Mineiro&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Kits">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The club's home kit has always consisted of a black-and-white vertically striped shirt, with black shorts and white or black socks. The width of the black and white stripes has varied from season to season, as has the colour of the shirt numbers, which have usually been red, black, white or yellow. Atlético's traditional away kit is all-white shirts, shorts and socks, but has had slight variations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-kits_87-0"><a href="#cite_note-kits-87">[87]</a></sup> An all-black <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Third_kit" title="Third kit">third kit</a> was introduced in the 2000 season, being used again in 2015.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup> In 2008, a black-and-gold vertically striped third kit was launched to commemorate the club's centenary, featuring the first crest.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup> Squad number 12 is retired from the club's kits, dedicated to the <a href="/wiki/12th_man_(football)" title="12th man (football)">fans</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:4_90-0"><a href="#cite_note-:4-90">[90]</a></sup></p>
<p>Since the 1981 season, the club has had its kits manufactured by sportswear corporations, the first one being Brazilian company Rainha.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:11_91-0"><a href="#cite_note-:11-91">[91]</a></sup> Atlético's kits will be manufactured in 2017 by <a href="/wiki/Topper_(sports)" title="Topper (sports)">Topper</a>, a company which had previously provided apparel for the club from 2010 to 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup> Other previous suppliers were <a href="/wiki/Adidas" title="Adidas">Adidas</a> (1983–85), <a href="/wiki/Penalty_(sports_manufacturer)" title="Penalty (sports manufacturer)">Penalty</a> (1986–90, 1992–93 and 1997–2001),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:11_91-1"><a href="#cite_note-:11-91">[91]</a></sup> Dell'erba (1991), <a href="/wiki/Umbro" title="Umbro">Umbro</a> (1994–96 and 2002–04),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:12_94-0"><a href="#cite_note-:12-94">[94]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Diadora" title="Diadora">Diadora</a> (2005–07), <a href="/wiki/Lotto_Sport_Italia" title="Lotto Sport Italia">Lotto</a> (2008–09), Lupo (2013),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Puma_SE" title="Puma SE">Puma</a> (2014–2015) and <a href="/wiki/Dryworld" title="Dryworld">Dryworld</a> (2016).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-puma_96-0"><a href="#cite_note-puma-96">[96]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1982, bank Credireal was Atlético's first shirt sponsor.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:11_91-2"><a href="#cite_note-:11-91">[91]</a></sup> After one sponsorless season in 1983, Precon, a construction company, appeared on the shirts in 1984 and 1985; it was replaced by Agrimisa bank in 1986. In 1987, <a href="/wiki/The_Coca-Cola_Company" title="The Coca-Cola Company">Coca-Cola</a> sponsored all participating clubs of <a href="/wiki/Copa_Uni%C3%A3o" title="Copa União">Copa União</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup> and the brand remained on Atlético's kits until 1994. The club was subsequently sponsored by <a href="/wiki/LATAM_Brasil" title="LATAM Brasil">TAM Airlines</a> (1995–96), <a href="/wiki/Construtora_Tenda" title="Construtora Tenda">Tenda</a> (1997–98),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:12_94-1"><a href="#cite_note-:12-94">[94]</a></sup> and had temporary deals with <a href="/wiki/Fiat_Chrysler_Automobiles" title="Fiat Chrysler Automobiles">Fiat</a> and <a href="/wiki/Oi_(telecommunications)" title="Oi (telecommunications)">Telemar</a> in 1999.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup> Two sponsorless years followed, before permanent deals were signed with Fiat (2002–03), <a href="/wiki/MRV_Engenharia" title="MRV Engenharia">MRV Engenharia</a> (2004–07) and Fiat again in 2008.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup> After one more season without a brand on the club's shirts, BMG, a bank that was owned by the former club president Ricardo Annes Guimarães,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup> was the main sponsor from 2010 to 2014. MRV returned as the club's main shirt sponsor in 2015,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup> being replaced by state-owned bank <a href="/wiki/Caixa_Econ%C3%B4mica_Federal" title="Caixa Econômica Federal">Caixa Econômica Federal</a> in 2016.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-caixa_104-0"><a href="#cite_note-caixa-104">[104]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Grounds">Grounds</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Clube_Atl%C3%A9tico_Mineiro&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Grounds">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Mineir%C3%A3o" title="Mineirão">Mineirão</a>, <a href="/wiki/Est%C3%A1dio_Independ%C3%AAncia" title="Estádio Independência">Estádio Independência</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Est%C3%A1dio_Presidente_Ant%C3%B4nio_Carlos" title="Estádio Presidente Antônio Carlos">Estádio Presidente Antônio Carlos</a></div>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">For the training grounds, see <a href="/wiki/Cidade_do_Galo" title="Cidade do Galo">Cidade do Galo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vila_Ol%C3%ADmpica" title="Vila Olímpica">Vila Olímpica</a>.</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Estadio_Antonio_Carlos.jpg"><img alt="Stadium stand, photographed from the pitch" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="300" data-file-width="620" height="106" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Estadio_Antonio_Carlos.jpg/220px-Estadio_Antonio_Carlos.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Estadio_Antonio_Carlos.jpg/330px-Estadio_Antonio_Carlos.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Estadio_Antonio_Carlos.jpg/440px-Estadio_Antonio_Carlos.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Estadio_Antonio_Carlos.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Estádio Presidente Antônio Carlos was Atlético Mineiro's home ground from 1929 to 1950.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Atlético had its first home ground built in 1912 at Paraopeba Avenue, in downtown Belo Horizonte, across the street from <a href="/wiki/Am%C3%A9rica_Futebol_Clube_(MG)" title="América Futebol Clube (MG)">América</a>'s first stadium.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup> The club's main ground for most of its early years, however, was the <a href="/wiki/Est%C3%A1dio_Presidente_Ant%C3%B4nio_Carlos" title="Estádio Presidente Antônio Carlos">Presidente Antônio Carlos stadium</a>, which held 5,000 people; it was nicknamed <i>Estádio de Lourdes</i> for the quarter in which it was located. The Antônio Carlos was one of the first stadiums in Brazil to feature <a href="/wiki/Floodlight" title="Floodlight">floodlights</a>, and opened on 30 May 1929 with a friendly against <a href="/wiki/Sport_Club_Corinthians_Paulista" title="Sport Club Corinthians Paulista">Corinthians</a>, won by Atlético 4–2. The following year, the stadium was visited by <a href="/wiki/FIFA" title="FIFA">FIFA</a> president <a href="/wiki/Jules_Rimet" title="Jules Rimet">Jules Rimet</a>, who watched a <a href="/wiki/Night_game" title="Night game">night game</a> for the first time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-clubs_106-0"><a href="#cite_note-clubs-106">[106]</a></sup> The stadium fell out of favour when the larger <a href="/wiki/Est%C3%A1dio_Independ%C3%AAncia" title="Estádio Independência">Independência</a> was built in 1950, and remained largely unused by the first team; eventually it was sold by the club to the Belo Horizonte municipality in the 1960s. After decades of legal disputes with the municipal government, the property returned to the club in 1991. It was leased to a shopping mall in 1995, which was built in the following year where the stadium once was, across the street from Atlético's administrative headquarters.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Arena_Independ%C3%AAncia_-_Atl%C3%A9tico_x_Fluminense.jpg"><img alt="Stadium interior with supporters, photographed from one of its corners" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="432" data-file-width="768" height="124" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Arena_Independ%C3%AAncia_-_Atl%C3%A9tico_x_Fluminense.jpg/220px-Arena_Independ%C3%AAncia_-_Atl%C3%A9tico_x_Fluminense.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Arena_Independ%C3%AAncia_-_Atl%C3%A9tico_x_Fluminense.jpg/330px-Arena_Independ%C3%AAncia_-_Atl%C3%A9tico_x_Fluminense.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Arena_Independ%C3%AAncia_-_Atl%C3%A9tico_x_Fluminense.jpg/440px-Arena_Independ%C3%AAncia_-_Atl%C3%A9tico_x_Fluminense.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Arena_Independ%C3%AAncia_-_Atl%C3%A9tico_x_Fluminense.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Independência, the club's first choice home stadium from 1950 to 1965, and since 2012.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Construction for the Independência (officially Estádio Raimundo Sampaio) started in 1947 in preparation for the <a href="/wiki/1950_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1950 FIFA World Cup">1950 FIFA World Cup</a>, during which its first match was played.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup> Originally the property of the State Government of Minas Gerais, ownership was transferred to Sete de Setembro FC in 1965, when the <a href="/wiki/Mineir%C3%A3o" title="Mineirão">Mineirão</a> was built, and the property passed to América in 1997, when it absorbed Sete de Setembro.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup> Before the Mineirão, the stadium was the largest in Belo Horizonte — holding up to 30,000 people — and was preferred by Atlético over the older and smaller Antônio Carlos stadium. After the Mineirão's construction, however, Atlético did not use the <i>Estádio do Horto</i> (as it is also known) for decades, except for a brief spell in the late 1990s. The stadium was renovated in 2012, while the Mineirão was closed, having its capacity reduced to 23,018. In that year, Atlético announced a deal with BWA Arenas, the stadium manager. The club signed a contract to use the Independência as its home ground for 10 years, which has happened since then, except in important and high-attendance matches.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hist.C3.B3ria_-_Atl.C3.A9tico_18-1"><a href="#cite_note-Hist.C3.B3ria_-_Atl.C3.A9tico-18">[18]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mineirao_Stadium.jpg"><img alt="Stadium interior, photographed from behind one of the goals" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="560" data-file-width="784" height="157" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Mineirao_Stadium.jpg/220px-Mineirao_Stadium.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Mineirao_Stadium.jpg/330px-Mineirao_Stadium.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Mineirao_Stadium.jpg/440px-Mineirao_Stadium.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mineirao_Stadium.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Mineirão, Atlético's ground for most of its history, was renovated for the <a href="/wiki/2014_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2014 FIFA World Cup">2014 FIFA World Cup</a> and is used for important matches.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Mineirão (officially Estádio Governador Magalhães Pinto) opened in 1965, and quickly became the home of both Atlético and Cruzeiro,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup> as its peak capacity of over 100,000 spectators surpassed any other stadium in Belo Horizonte or in the state. The property of the state of Minas Gerais, Mineirão was Atlético's home from its opening until it closed in 2010 for renovations prior to the <a href="/wiki/2014_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2014 FIFA World Cup">2014 FIFA World Cup</a>. The club temporarily moved to <a href="/wiki/Arena_do_Jacar%C3%A9" title="Arena do Jacaré">Arena do Jacaré</a> in <a href="/wiki/Sete_Lagoas" title="Sete Lagoas">Sete Lagoas</a> and subsequently to Independência in 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup> Historically the club's home ground, Atlético's most important matches have all been played at the Mineirão, a fact that has continued even after Independência became the first-choice home stadium again.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup> After the renovation, the Mineirão has an overall capacity of 61,846.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cnef_2-1"><a href="#cite_note-cnef-2">[2]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Cidade_do_Galo" title="Cidade do Galo">Cidade do Galo</a> ("Rooster City"), the club's main training facility since 2001, has been lauded as the best in Brazil and is considered one of the best in the world;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup> it hosted the <a href="/wiki/Argentina_national_football_team" title="Argentina national football team">Argentina national football team</a> at the 2014 FIFA World Cup.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup> Other facilities owned by the club include <a href="/wiki/Vila_Ol%C3%ADmpica" title="Vila Olímpica">Vila Olímpica</a> ("Olympic Village"), the old training grounds opened in 1973 that hosted the <i>Seleção</i> in its preparation for the <a href="/wiki/1982_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1982 FIFA World Cup">1982 FIFA World Cup</a>, and <i>Labareda</i>, a leisure and health club in Belo Horizonte.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-clubs_106-1"><a href="#cite_note-clubs-106">[106]</a></sup> In 2015, Daniel Nepomuceno, the club president, announced that Atlético had a four-year project to build a new stadium in Belo Horizonte, with a 45,000 capacity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Supporters">Supporters</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Clube_Atl%C3%A9tico_Mineiro&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Supporters">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mineir%C3%A3o_-_Libertadores_2013.jpg"><img alt="Football crowd inside a stadium" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="960" data-file-width="1280" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Mineir%C3%A3o_-_Libertadores_2013.jpg/220px-Mineir%C3%A3o_-_Libertadores_2013.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Mineir%C3%A3o_-_Libertadores_2013.jpg/330px-Mineir%C3%A3o_-_Libertadores_2013.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Mineir%C3%A3o_-_Libertadores_2013.jpg/440px-Mineir%C3%A3o_-_Libertadores_2013.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mineir%C3%A3o_-_Libertadores_2013.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<i>A massa</i> supporting Atlético Mineiro at the <a href="/wiki/Mineir%C3%A3o" title="Mineirão">Mineirão</a> in 2013</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Atlético Mineiro was founded by upper-class students, but from an early age it opened its doors to players from every social class, nationality or ethnicity, which earned it a "people's club" status in Belo Horizonte and in the state. América, meanwhile, had a reputation as an elitist club, and Cruzeiro was strongly associated with the local Italian colony.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pc1_5-1"><a href="#cite_note-pc1-5">[5]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pc2_6-1"><a href="#cite_note-pc2-6">[6]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup> As a result of the popular support, the fans came to be collectively known as <i>"A Massa"</i> (Portuguese for "the mass").<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup> According to a 2014 survey conducted by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/IBOPE" title="IBOPE">IBOPE</a> and <i><a href="/wiki/Lance!" title="Lance!">Lance!</a></i>, the club is the best-supported in Belo Horizonte and in Minas Gerais, and has the sixth largest fanbase in Brazil, with seven million supporters.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:2_8-1"><a href="#cite_note-:2-8">[8]</a></sup> A 2014 survey by <a href="/wiki/Datafolha" title="Datafolha">Datafolha</a>, however, shows Atlético as the second best-supported club in Minas Gerais and tenth in Brazil.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup></p>
<p>Atlético has many <a href="/wiki/Torcida_organizada" title="Torcida organizada"><i>torcidas organizadas</i></a> that support the club, the oldest being <i>Dragões da FAO</i>, founded in 1969, and the largest and best-known being <i>Galoucura</i>. Other notable groups include <i>Galö Metal</i>, <i>Movimento 105 Minutos</i> and the <i>Charanga</i>, a <a href="/wiki/Brass_band" title="Brass band">brass band</a> that plays during the club's home matches.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup> Galoucura has historically developed alliances with other <i>torcidas</i> in Brazil, most notably <a href="/wiki/Sociedade_Esportiva_Palmeiras" title="Sociedade Esportiva Palmeiras">Palmeiras</a>'s <i>Mancha Verde</i> and <a href="/wiki/CR_Vasco_da_Gama" title="CR Vasco da Gama">Vasco da Gama</a>'s <i>Força Jovem</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup> After difficult but successful comebacks in 2013 and 2014, the fans have adopted the motto <i>"Eu acredito"</i> ("I believe") to support the club in against-the-odds situations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125"><a href="#cite_note-125">[125]</a></sup> Squad number 12 is retired from the club's kits and dedicated to the fans.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:4_90-1"><a href="#cite_note-:4-90">[90]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:442px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Clube_Atl%C3%A9tico_Mineiro_average_attendance_chart.png"><img alt="Line graph" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="400" data-file-width="850" height="207" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Clube_Atl%C3%A9tico_Mineiro_average_attendance_chart.png/440px-Clube_Atl%C3%A9tico_Mineiro_average_attendance_chart.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Clube_Atl%C3%A9tico_Mineiro_average_attendance_chart.png/660px-Clube_Atl%C3%A9tico_Mineiro_average_attendance_chart.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/4/43/Clube_Atl%C3%A9tico_Mineiro_average_attendance_chart.png 2x" width="440"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Clube_Atl%C3%A9tico_Mineiro_average_attendance_chart.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Chart with Atlético Mineiro's average attendances in the national league from 1971 to 2015</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Atlético has had the best average attendance in nine editions of the Série A since 1972, and has the second highest all-time average attendance in Brazilian football.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup> The club also ranks second in all-time total attendance in the national league, with more than 13 million tickets sold in 581 home matches as of the 2014 season.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127"><a href="#cite_note-127">[127]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128"><a href="#cite_note-128">[128]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129"><a href="#cite_note-129">[129]</a></sup> The second leg of the <a href="/wiki/2013_Copa_Libertadores_Finals" title="2013 Copa Libertadores Finals">2013 Copa Libertadores finals</a> between Atlético and Olimpia, played at the Mineirão and attended by 58,620 people, had the highest gate receipt revenue of all time in South American football, yielding <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_real" title="Brazilian real">R$</a>14.2 million (€4.8 million at the time).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130"><a href="#cite_note-130">[130]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1999, the club introduced <i>Galo de Prata</i> ("Silver Rooster"), a trophy officially awarded by Atlético to sportspeople, illustrious supporters, artists, politicians, and organisations that somehow promote the club's name.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup> Since the implementation of municipal and state laws in 2007 and 2008, <i>Dia do Atleticano</i> ("Atleticano Day") is officially celebrated in Belo Horizonte and Minas Gerais every year on 25 March, the day of the club's foundation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132"><a href="#cite_note-132">[132]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-133"><a href="#cite_note-133">[133]</a></sup> Atlético launched <a href="/wiki/TV_Galo" title="TV Galo">TV Galo</a> in 2007, a <a href="/wiki/Pay_television" title="Pay television">premium television channel</a> that provides content for fans such as interviews with players and staff, coverage of training sessions and matches, footballing news, and other themed programming.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134"><a href="#cite_note-134">[134]</a></sup> Since 2012, the club has an affiliation programme called <i>Galo na Veia,</i> in which supporters can become season ticket holders or pay monthly fees to buy match tickets at reduced price.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-135"><a href="#cite_note-135">[135]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Rivalries">Rivalries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Clube_Atl%C3%A9tico_Mineiro&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Rivalries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Cl%C3%A1ssico_Mineiro" title="Clássico Mineiro">Clássico Mineiro</a>, <a href="/wiki/Am%C3%A9rica_Futebol_Clube%E2%80%93Clube_Atl%C3%A9tico_Mineiro_rivalry" title="América Futebol Clube–Clube Atlético Mineiro rivalry">América Futebol Clube–Clube Atlético Mineiro rivalry</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Clube_de_Regatas_do_Flamengo%E2%80%93Clube_Atl%C3%A9tico_Mineiro_rivalry" title="Clube de Regatas do Flamengo–Clube Atlético Mineiro rivalry">Clube de Regatas do Flamengo–Clube Atlético Mineiro rivalry</a></div>
<p>The local rivalry between Atlético and Cruzeiro, known as the <i><a href="/wiki/Cl%C3%A1ssico_Mineiro" title="Clássico Mineiro">Clássico Mineiro</a></i> ("Mineiro Derby"), exists since Cruzeiro's foundation (as Sociedade Esportiva Palestra Itália) in 1921. It strengthened in the 1940s, and became the biggest derby in Minas Gerais in the 1960s.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pc2_6-2"><a href="#cite_note-pc2-6">[6]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136"><a href="#cite_note-136">[136]</a></sup> Atlético dominated the rivalry from its early days until the 1950s, but Cruzeiro rose in the 1960s to be a strong challenger, and the 1970s had divided honours.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137"><a href="#cite_note-137">[137]</a></sup> The 1980s were dominated by Atlético, while the 1990s and 2000s were favourable to Cruzeiro. The 2010s have the rivals competing at an even level. The clubs dissent over the number of matches and head-to-head record of the <i>Clássico Mineiro</i>, but both team's statistics show Atlético with most wins in the encounter.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-138"><a href="#cite_note-138">[138]</a></sup> The only national final between the two clubs happened in the <a href="/wiki/2014_Copa_do_Brasil" title="2014 Copa do Brasil">2014 Copa do Brasil</a>, when Atlético triumphed in a final match played at the Mineirão.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FourFourTwo_73-1"><a href="#cite_note-FourFourTwo-73">[73]</a></sup> The <i>Clássico</i>'s most extreme result was a <a href="/wiki/Atl%C3%A9tico_Mineiro_9%E2%80%932_Cruzeiro_(1927)" title="Atlético Mineiro 9–2 Cruzeiro (1927)">9–2 win by Atlético</a>, in the 1927 Campeonato Mineiro.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139"><a href="#cite_note-139">[139]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-140"><a href="#cite_note-140">[140]</a></sup></p>
<p>Atlético versus América was known as the <i>Clássico das Multidões</i> ("Derby of the Masses") before the construction of the Mineirão, as they were the most popular clubs in the state.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-141"><a href="#cite_note-141">[141]</a></sup> In their first years, América was known as an elitist club, while Atlético had popular appeal;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pc1_5-2"><a href="#cite_note-pc1-5">[5]</a></sup> the former dominated the early years of the encounter, winning ten consecutive Campeonato Mineiro titles from 1916 to 1925. In the 1930s, Atlético pioneered <a href="/wiki/Professionalism_in_association_football" title="Professionalism in association football">professionalization of football</a> in Minas Gerais, whereas América resisted against it. From that time on, Galo became the major force between the two, with América suffering a setback as a result of its internal disagreements regarding professionalism.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142"><a href="#cite_note-142">[142]</a></sup></p>
<p>Atlético also holds a rivalry with <a href="/wiki/Clube_de_Regatas_do_Flamengo" title="Clube de Regatas do Flamengo">Flamengo</a> of <a href="/wiki/Rio_de_Janeiro" title="Rio de Janeiro">Rio de Janeiro</a>, with the first match between the clubs being played in 1929. Until regular national competitions were introduced in Brazilian football in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1959_Ta%C3%A7a_Brasil" title="1959 Taça Brasil">1959</a>, however, the encounters were played at friendly level, since the clubs are from different states. The rivalry developed in the 1980s, rising from numerous controversial encounters between the two clubs in Campeonato Brasileiro and Copa Libertadores editions of the period. It remained through the following decades, and is considered the biggest interstate rivalry in Brazilian football.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-143"><a href="#cite_note-143">[143]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Records_and_statistics">Records and statistics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Clube_Atl%C3%A9tico_Mineiro&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Records and statistics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bernard_2012_01.jpg"><img alt="Player on the pitch" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="507" data-file-width="308" height="362" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Bernard_2012_01.jpg/220px-Bernard_2012_01.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/2/27/Bernard_2012_01.jpg 1.5x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bernard_2012_01.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Bernard_(footballer)" title="Bernard (footballer)">Bernard</a>, who won the <a href="/wiki/2013_Copa_Libertadores" title="2013 Copa Libertadores">2013 Copa Libertadores</a> with Atlético, is the club's record sale.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Clube_Atl%C3%A9tico_Mineiro_records_and_statistics" title="List of Clube Atlético Mineiro records and statistics">List of Clube Atlético Mineiro records and statistics</a></div>
