<p><a href="/wiki/Jo%C3%A3o_Leite_da_Silva_Neto" title="João Leite da Silva Neto">João Leite</a> holds Atlético's official appearance record, with 684 matches in all competitions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-144"><a href="#cite_note-144">[144]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Reinaldo_de_Lima" title="José Reinaldo de Lima">Reinaldo</a> is the club's all-time leading goalscorer, with 255 goals, since joining the first squad in 1973.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-145"><a href="#cite_note-145">[145]</a></sup> In the 1977 season, he scored 28 goals in 18 appearances, setting the club record for the most Campeonato Brasileiro goals in a season, and the league's best average goal-per-game record (1.55).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_146-0"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-146">[146]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Dad%C3%A1_Maravilha" title="Dadá Maravilha">Dadá Maravilha</a> is second in total goals, with 211, and the only other Atlético player to score over 200 goals.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-147"><a href="#cite_note-147">[147]</a></sup> Argentine striker <a href="/wiki/Lucas_Pratto" title="Lucas Pratto">Lucas Pratto</a> is Atlético's all-time top foreign goalscorer, with 41 goals.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-148"><a href="#cite_note-148">[148]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-149"><a href="#cite_note-149">[149]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Tel%C3%AA_Santana" title="Telê Santana">Telê Santana</a> is Galo's longest-serving head coach, having taken charge of the team for 434 matches during three periods in the 1970s and 1980s.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-150"><a href="#cite_note-150">[150]</a></sup> Nelson Campos is the club's longest-serving president, with nine years in the office in three terms.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-151"><a href="#cite_note-151">[151]</a></sup></p>
<p>The first official game in which Atlético participated was against <a href="/wiki/Yale_Atl%C3%A9tico_Clube" title="Yale Atlético Clube">Yale</a> for the 1915 Campeonato Mineiro, which the team won 5–0.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-152"><a href="#cite_note-152">[152]</a></sup> The biggest victory ever recorded by Galo was 13–0, against Calafate in the 1927 Campeonato Mineiro. In the national league, the biggest win came against <a href="/wiki/Associa%C3%A7%C3%A3o_Desportiva_Ferrovi%C3%A1ria_Vale_do_Rio_Doce" title="Associação Desportiva Ferroviária Vale do Rio Doce">Desportiva Ferroviária</a> — 7–1 in the <a href="/wiki/1982_Campeonato_Brasileiro_S%C3%A9rie_A" title="1982 Campeonato Brasileiro Série A">1982 season</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-153"><a href="#cite_note-153">[153]</a></sup> Atlético's biggest win in the Copa do Brasil, 11–0 against <a href="/wiki/Cai%C3%A7ara_Esporte_Clube" title="Caiçara Esporte Clube">Caiçara</a> in <a href="/wiki/1991_Copa_do_Brasil" title="1991 Copa do Brasil">1991</a>, is also the competition's record victory.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-154"><a href="#cite_note-154">[154]</a></sup> The club's home attendance record — split-crowd derbies excepted — is 115,142, in a friendly against Flamengo at the Mineirão, in 1980. The record attendance in official matches is 113,749, achieved in a match against <a href="/wiki/Santos_FC" title="Santos FC">Santos</a> for the <a href="/wiki/1983_Campeonato_Brasileiro_S%C3%A9rie_A" title="1983 Campeonato Brasileiro Série A">1983 Brasileirão</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-155"><a href="#cite_note-155">[155]</a></sup> Atlético holds the Brazilian record for longest unbeaten run at home, with 54 matches from 2011 to 2013.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-156"><a href="#cite_note-156">[156]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-157"><a href="#cite_note-157">[157]</a></sup> The signing of <a href="/wiki/Andr%C3%A9_Felipe_Ribeiro_de_Souza" title="André Felipe Ribeiro de Souza">André</a> from <a href="/wiki/FC_Dynamo_Kyiv" title="FC Dynamo Kyiv">Dynamo Kyiv</a> in 2012 is the club's most expensive purchase, costing around €8 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-158"><a href="#cite_note-158">[158]</a></sup> Atlético's record sale is the transfer of <a href="/wiki/Bernard_(footballer)" title="Bernard (footballer)">Bernard</a> to <a href="/wiki/FC_Shakhtar_Donetsk" title="FC Shakhtar Donetsk">Shakhtar Donetsk</a> in 2013, which cost the Ukrainian club €25 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-159"><a href="#cite_note-159">[159]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Organisation_and_finances">Organisation and finances</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Clube_Atl%C3%A9tico_Mineiro&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Organisation and finances">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>As is the case for most Brazilian football clubs, Atlético Mineiro's <a href="/wiki/By-law" title="By-law">by-law</a> defines the club as a <a href="/wiki/Nonprofit_organization" title="Nonprofit organization">not-for-profit public utility organization</a>, formed by associates (<i>sócios</i>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-estatuto_160-0"><a href="#cite_note-estatuto-160">[160]</a></sup> The club's administrative powers are the General Assembly, the Deliberative Council, the Board, the Fiscal Council and the Ethics and Discipline Council. The General Assembly, composed of all associates, elects the Deliberative Council among its members every three years, which in turn elects and removes the club's Board, responsible for the executive management of the club.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-estatuto_160-1"><a href="#cite_note-estatuto-160">[160]</a></sup> Season ticket-holders and participants of the <i>Galo na Veia</i> affiliation programme, called <i>sócios-torcedores</i>, are not full club associates and cannot vote or be elected.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-161"><a href="#cite_note-161">[161]</a></sup></p>
<p>A study conducted by <a href="/wiki/BDO_International" title="BDO International">BDO</a> in 2016 indicated that the club had a brand value of <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_real" title="Brazilian real">R$</a>515.5 million (€143 million), making it the eighth most valuable in Brazil.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:6_12-1"><a href="#cite_note-:6-12">[12]</a></sup> In terms of annual turnover, Atlético ranked seventh in the country in 2015, earning R$244.6 million (€62.2 million), which represented a 37 per cent increase compared to the previous year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:6_12-2"><a href="#cite_note-:6-12">[12]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-balancesheet_162-0"><a href="#cite_note-balancesheet-162">[162]</a></sup> The club has a main sponsorship deal with <a href="/wiki/Caixa_Econ%C3%B4mica_Federal" title="Caixa Econômica Federal">Caixa Econômica Federal</a>, worth R$12.5 million (€3.2 million) annually.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-caixa_104-1"><a href="#cite_note-caixa-104">[104]</a></sup> Its kit sponsorship deal with <a href="/wiki/Dryworld" title="Dryworld">Dryworld</a>, worth R$20 million (€5.1 million) per year, is the third biggest in the country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-163"><a href="#cite_note-163">[163]</a></sup></p>
<p>The club's gross debt as of 2015 was R$496.5 million (€126.6 million), the third largest in Brazil, with a R$11.9 million (€3 million) deficit in the same year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:6_12-3"><a href="#cite_note-:6-12">[12]</a></sup> The club's balance sheet in that year stated it experienced operational losses, and according to a study by <a href="/wiki/Ita%C3%BA_Unibanco" title="Itaú Unibanco">Itaú BBA</a>, Atlético operates in a dangerous "financial all-in".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-balancesheet_162-1"><a href="#cite_note-balancesheet-162">[162]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-164"><a href="#cite_note-164">[164]</a></sup> The majority of the club's debt is owed to the <a href="/wiki/Federal_government_of_Brazil" title="Federal government of Brazil">Federal Government of Brazil</a>, totalling R$286.6 million (€89.1 million); in 2015, Atlético and other clubs joined a government programme for debt financing.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-165"><a href="#cite_note-165">[165]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="In_popular_culture">In popular culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Clube_Atl%C3%A9tico_Mineiro&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: In popular culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Atlético Mineiro and episodes in the club's history have appeared on films and other media. The <a href="/wiki/Music_video" title="Music video">music video</a> for "É Uma Partida de Futebol" ("It's a Football Match"), by Brazilian rock band <a href="/wiki/Skank_(band)" title="Skank (band)">Skank</a>, was filmed during a 1997 <i>Clássico Mineiro</i> match between Atlético and Cruzeiro; the video won three categories at the 1997 <a href="/wiki/MTV_Video_Music_Brazil" title="MTV Video Music Brazil">MTV Video Music Brazil</a> awards.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-166"><a href="#cite_note-166">[166]</a></sup> An Atlético match was also depicted in a <a href="/wiki/Martian_Manhunter" title="Martian Manhunter">Martian Manhunter</a> comic book, by <a href="/wiki/DC_Comics" title="DC Comics">DC Comics</a>, in 2015.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-167"><a href="#cite_note-167">[167]</a></sup> The protagonist in <i><a href="/wiki/Memories_of_the_Desert" title="Memories of the Desert">Memories of the Desert</a></i>, a 2014 Brazilian crime drama film, is a supporter of the club (as is the actor who portrayed him, <a href="/wiki/Daniel_de_Oliveira_(actor)" title="Daniel de Oliveira (actor)">Daniel de Oliveira</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-168"><a href="#cite_note-168">[168]</a></sup></p>
<p>A <a href="/wiki/Short_film" title="Short film">short film</a> about goalkeeper Victor's iconic penalty-kick save against Tijuana in the 2013 Copa Libertadores was released in 2014; named <i>A Dream You Dream Together Is Reality</i>, it was awarded the <i>Guirlande D'Honneur</i> by the International Sport Movies TV Federation (FICTS).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-169"><a href="#cite_note-169">[169]</a></sup> In the following year, <i><a href="/wiki/O_Dia_do_Galo" title="O Dia do Galo">O Dia do Galo</a></i>, a documentary that followed five Atlético supporters on the day of the final match of the same competition, was released in theatres as a <a href="/wiki/Feature_film" title="Feature film">feature film</a>. The motion picture was one of the most watched Brazilian films of 2015, and won the Popular Jury award at the Mostra de Cinema de Tiradentes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-170"><a href="#cite_note-170">[170]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-171"><a href="#cite_note-171">[171]</a></sup> <i>O Imortal do Gelo</i>, a film about the club's 1950 tour to Europe, was released in 2015.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-172"><a href="#cite_note-172">[172]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Honours">Honours</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Clube_Atl%C3%A9tico_Mineiro&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Honours">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">For more details on this topic, see <a href="/wiki/List_of_Clube_Atl%C3%A9tico_Mineiro_records_and_statistics#Honours" title="List of Clube Atlético Mineiro records and statistics">List of Clube Atlético Mineiro records and statistics § Honours</a>.</div>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Clube_Atl%C3%A9tico_Mineiro_seasons" title="List of Clube Atlético Mineiro seasons">List of Clube Atlético Mineiro seasons</a> and <a href="/wiki/Clube_Atl%C3%A9tico_Mineiro_in_international_club_football" title="Clube Atlético Mineiro in international club football">Clube Atlético Mineiro in international club football</a></div>
<p>Atlético Mineiro's first trophy was the Taça Bueno Brandão, won in 1914. The club was the first winner of the <a href="/wiki/Campeonato_Mineiro" title="Campeonato Mineiro">Campeonato Mineiro</a>, the state league of Minas Gerais, a competition it has won a record 43 times; it has also won the <a href="/wiki/Ta%C3%A7a_Minas_Gerais" title="Taça Minas Gerais">Taça Minas Gerais</a>, a state cup, on five occasions. At national level, Atlético has won the <a href="/wiki/Campeonato_Brasileiro_S%C3%A9rie_A" title="Campeonato Brasileiro Série A">Campeonato Brasileiro</a> once, while finishing second on five seasons; it has also won the <a href="/wiki/Copa_dos_Campe%C3%B5es_Estaduais" title="Copa dos Campeões Estaduais">Copa dos Campeões Estaduais</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Copa_dos_Campe%C3%B5es_da_Copa_Brasil" title="Copa dos Campeões da Copa Brasil">Copa dos Campeões Brasileiros</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Copa_do_Brasil" title="Copa do Brasil">Copa do Brasil</a> once each, also finishing as runner-up once in the latter. In international competitions, Atlético has won the <a href="/wiki/Copa_Libertadores" title="Copa Libertadores">Copa Libertadores</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Recopa_Sudamericana" title="Recopa Sudamericana">Recopa Sudamericana</a> once each, and a record two <a href="/wiki/Copa_CONMEBOL" title="Copa CONMEBOL">Copa CONMEBOL</a> trophies; the club has also finished as runner-up of the Copa CONMEBOL, the <a href="/wiki/Copa_de_Oro" title="Copa de Oro">Copa de Oro</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Copa_Master_de_CONMEBOL" title="Copa Master de CONMEBOL">Copa Master de CONMEBOL</a>. The club has competed in the <a href="/wiki/FIFA_Club_World_Cup" title="FIFA Club World Cup">FIFA Club World Cup</a> once, finishing in third place. The club's most recent title is the <a href="/wiki/2015_Campeonato_Mineiro" title="2015 Campeonato Mineiro">2015 Campeonato Mineiro</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-173"><a href="#cite_note-173">[173]</a></sup></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Players">Players</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Clube_Atl%C3%A9tico_Mineiro&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Players">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Club_board">Club board</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Clube_Atl%C3%A9tico_Mineiro&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Club board">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_departments">Other departments</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Clube_Atl%C3%A9tico_Mineiro&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Other departments">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Futsal">Futsal</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Clube_Atl%C3%A9tico_Mineiro&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Futsal">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Atlético Mineiro opened its <a href="/wiki/Futsal" title="Futsal">futsal</a> department in the 1960s, achieving victories at state level in the following decades, and winning the <a href="/wiki/Ta%C3%A7a_Brasil_de_Futsal" title="Taça Brasil de Futsal">Taça Brasil</a> in 1985.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-183"><a href="#cite_note-183">[183]</a></sup> In the late 1990s, the team, named Atlético Pax de Minas for sponsorship reasons, was prominent at national and international level. With players such as <a href="/wiki/Manoel_Tobias" title="Manoel Tobias">Manoel Tobias</a>, <a href="/wiki/Falc%C3%A3o_(futsal_player)" title="Falcão (futsal player)">Falcão</a> and <a href="/wiki/Len%C3%ADsio" title="Lenísio">Lenísio</a> in the squad, Atlético won the Brazilian <a href="/wiki/Liga_Futsal" title="Liga Futsal">Liga Futsal</a> twice, in 1997 and 1999, and the <a href="/wiki/Intercontinental_Futsal_Cup" title="Intercontinental Futsal Cup">Intercontinental Futsal Cup</a> in 1998, being runner-up of both competitions in 2000.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-184"><a href="#cite_note-184">[184]</a></sup> In the second leg of the 1999 Liga Futsal finals against Rio de Janeiro, the attendance at <a href="/wiki/Mineirinho" title="Mineirinho">Mineirinho</a> was 25,713, a world record in the sport.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-185"><a href="#cite_note-185">[185]</a></sup> In 2000, the sponsorship deal with Pax de Minas ended and Atlético's professional senior futsal team folded in the following year, with the youth sectors remaining.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-186"><a href="#cite_note-186">[186]</a></sup> The club's futsal department ceased operations in 2009.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-187"><a href="#cite_note-187">[187]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Olympic_sports">Olympic sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Clube_Atl%C3%A9tico_Mineiro&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Olympic sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Atlético Mineiro had departments for other <a href="/wiki/Olympic_sports" title="Olympic sports">Olympic sports</a> throughout its history, with the athletics and volleyball ones achieving notability. In 1983, runner João da Mata won the <a href="/wiki/Saint_Silvester_Road_Race" title="Saint Silvester Road Race">São Silvestre road race</a> as an Atlético athlete.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-188"><a href="#cite_note-188">[188]</a></sup> In 2007, <a href="/wiki/Robert_Kipkoech_Cheruiyot" title="Robert Kipkoech Cheruiyot">Robert Kipkoech Cheruiyot</a> and <a href="/wiki/Alice_Timbilil" title="Alice Timbilil">Alice Timbilil</a> won the male and female categories of the same race, and celebrated their victory with Atlético flags. The club's board stated that the athletes had been sponsored as a marketing strategy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-189"><a href="#cite_note-189">[189]</a></sup> Atlético's men's <a href="/wiki/Volleyball" title="Volleyball">volleyball</a> department won the <a href="/wiki/Minas_Gerais_Volleyball_Championship" title="Minas Gerais Volleyball Championship">Minas Gerais Volleyball Championship</a> a total of twelve times, ranking second in the state for most titles. The team had an especially successful period in the early 1980s, under the administrative management of Alexandre Kalil, who became club president in 2009.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-190"><a href="#cite_note-190">[190]</a></sup></p>
